        </div><div class="casAbstract">Little work has been done on the mechanism of low dose hyper-radiosensitivity (HRS) and later appeared radioresistance (termed induced radioresistance (IRR)) after irradn. with medium and high linear energy transfer (LET) particles.  The aim of this study was to find out whether ATR pathway is involved in the mechanism of HRS induced by high LET radiation.  GM0639 cells and two ATM deficient/mutant cells, AT5BIVA and AT2KY were irradiated by carbon ion beam.  Thymidine block technique was developed to enrich the G2-phase population.  Radiation induced early G2/M checkpoint was quant. assess with dual-parameter flow cytometry by detecting the cells pos. for phospho-histone H3.  The involvement of ATR pathway in HRS/IRR response was detected with pretreatment of specific inhibitors prior to carbon ion beam.  The link between the early G2/M checkpoint and HRS/IRR under carbon ion beam was first confirmed in GM0639 cells, through the enrichment of cell population in G2-phase or with Aurora kinase inhibitor that attenuates the transition from G2 to M phase.  Interestingly, the early G2/M arrest could still be obsd. in ATM deficient/mutant cells with an effect of ATR signaling, which was discovered to function in an LET-dependent manner, even as low as 0.2 Gy for carbon ion radiation.  The involvement of ATR pathway in heavy particles induced HRS/IRR was detd. with the specific ATR inhibitor in GM0639 cells, which affected the HRS/IRR occurrence similarly as ATM inhibitor.  These data demonstrate that ATR pathway may cooperate with ATM in the mechanism of low dose hypersensitivity induced by carbon ion beam.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-U5zigsww1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li3uvHntmWcBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1SgtLvN&amp;md5=2278b9b34d2f6e81c81639a7e011ef36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.10.143"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yeh, Y.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wongittharom, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tseng, C.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, W.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, J.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rechargeable Na/ Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> Cells with Ionic Liquid Electrolytes Containing Various Sodium Solutes</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Solid polymers electrolytes (SPEs) based on Na bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide (NaFSI) and poly(ethylene oxide) (PEO) with different ether O to Na (O:Na) molar ratios (n), resulting in NaFSI(PEO)n materials are here presented for the 1st time. While for the most dil. systems (n = 20) the two SPE families show similar ionic conductivities in the entire temp. range studied (273-343 K), for n = 6 and n = 9 they differ significantly; at room temp., the NaFSI based SPEs show lower ionic conductivities than the NaTFSI based analogs. SPE, NaFSI(PEO)6, and the NaFSI based SPEs in general to result in less free anions than the NaTFSI based SPEs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exptl. investigations on a sodium ion conducting gel polymer electrolyte nanocomposite based on poly(vinylidene fluoride-co-hexafluoropropylene) (PVdF-HFP), dispersed with silica nanoparticles are reported.  The gel nanocomposites have been obtained in the form of dimensionally stable, transparent and free-standing thick films.  Phys. characterization by X-ray diffraction (XRD), Fourier transform Infra-red (FTIR) spectroscopy and SEM (SEM) have been performed to study the structural changes and the ion-filler-polymer interactions due to the dispersion of SiO2 nanoparticles in gel electrolytes.  The highest ionic cond. of the electrolyte has been obsd. to be 4.1 Ã 10-3 S cm-1 at room temp. with â¼3 wt.% of SiO2 particles.  The temp. dependence of the ionic cond. has been found to be consistent with Vogel-Tammen-Fulcher (VTF) relationship in the temp. range from 40 to 70 Â°C.  The sodium ion conduction in the gel electrolyte film is confirmed from the cyclic voltammetry, impedance anal. and transport no. measurements.  The value of sodium ion transport no. (tNa+) of the gel electrolyte is significantly enhanced to a max. value of 0.52 on the 15 wt. % SiO2 dispersion.  The phys. and electrochem. analyses indicate the suitability of the gel electrolyte films in the sodium batteries.  A prototype sodium-sulfur battery, fabricated using optimized gel electrolyte, offers the first discharge capacity of â¼165 mAh g-1 of sulfur.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqhYN6DeWAo3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmonjjJkHLFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhtlaitLfM&amp;md5=eccfe79bbbe8ed6e415b672b33c15126</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1021/am200973k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishikawa, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Murata, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ito, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ohsawa, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fluorinated Ethylene Carbonate as Electrolyte Additive for Rechargeable Na Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. were performed for the redn. decompn. of solvents widely used in Li-ion secondary battery electrolytes, ethylene carbonate (EC), propylene carbonate (PC), di-Me carbonate (DMC), Et Me carbonate (EMC), and di-Et carbonate (DEC), including a typical electrolyte additive, vinylene carbonate (VC), at the level of B3LYP/6-311+G(2d,p), both in the gas phase and soln. using the polarizable conductor calcn. model.  In the gas phase, the 1st electron redn. for the cyclic carbonates and for the linear carbonates is exothermic and endothermic, resp., while the 2nd electron redn. is endothermic for all the compds. examd.  On the contrary, in soln. both 1st and 2nd electron redns. are exothermic for all the compds.  Among the solvents and the additive examd., the likelihood of undergoing the 1st electron redn. in soln. was found in the order of EC &gt; PC &gt; VC &gt; DMC &gt; EMC &gt; DEC with EC being the most likely reduced.  VC, however, is most likely to undergo the 2nd electron redn. among the compds., in the order of VC &gt; EC &gt; PC.  Based on the results, the exptl. demonstrated effectiveness of VC as an excellent electrolyte additive was discussed.  The bulk thermodn. properties of two dilithium alkylene glycol dicarbonates, dilithium ethylene glycol dicarbonate (Li-EDC) and dilithium 1,2-propylene glycol dicarbonate (Li-PDC), as the major component of solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) films were also examd. through mol. dynamics (MD) simulations to understand the stability of the SEI film.  Film produced from a decompn. of EC, modeled by Li-EDC, has a higher d., more cohesive energy, and less soly. to the solvent than the film produced from decompn. of PC, Li-PDC.  Further, MD simulations of the interface between the decompn. compd. and graphite suggested that Li-EDC has more favorable interactions with the graphite surface than Li-PDC.  The difference in the SEI film stability and the behavior of Li-ion battery cycling among the solvents were discussed in terms of the mol. structures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr0Gsu8rcV52bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmonjjJkHLFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXosFWjtA%253D%253D&amp;md5=f89049b6f12046501b459926a8967c6b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref64'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1149/2.0431711jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">VÃ¤li, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">JÃ¤nes, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lust, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Alkali-Metal Insertion Processes on Nanospheric Hard Carbon Electrodes: An Electrochemical Impedance Spectroscopy Study</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper describes the prepn. of NaxVO2 phases by electrochem. deintercalation.  The curves V = f(x) show that the process is reversible up to x = 0.5 and they indicate multiple single phase domains in the range 1 &lt; x &lt; 0.5.  Two single phases were successfully isolated for Na1/2VO2 and Na2/3VO2 compns.; the authors report here the 1st x-ray powder diffraction measurements of these phases.  They present a O'3-type monoclinic distortion of the O3 rhombohedral phase obsd. for Na1VO2.  The evolution of cell parameters with Na deintercalation is comparable with other AxMO2 layered oxides.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYtKHyy3LVlrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk9H8MzJF-mg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXivVGisrw%253D&amp;md5=f443243e7ccaf4e42e86f5a389bd437f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c4ee03192j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M. Chem. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">8837</span>â <span class="NLM_lpage">8842</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c4cp01089b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The mechanism of NaFePO4 (de)sodiation determined by in situ X-ray diffraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Galceran, Montserrat; Saurel, Damien; Acebedo, Begona; Roddatis, Vladimir V.; Martin, Egoitz; Rojo, Teofilo; Casas-Cabanas, Montse</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8837-8842</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The reaction mechanism occurring during the (de)intercalation of sodium into the host olivine FePO4 structure is thoroughly analyzed through a combination of structural and electrochem. methods.  In situ XRD expts. have confirmed that the charge and discharge reaction mechanisms are different and have revealed the existence of a solid soln. domain from 1 &lt; x &lt; 2/3 in NaxFePO4 upon charge.  The second part of the charge proceeds through a 2-phase reaction between Na2/3FePO4 and FePO4 with strongly varying soly. limits.  The strong cell mismatch between Na2/3FePO4 and FePO4 enhances the effects of the diffuse interface and therefore varying soly. limits are first obsd. here in micrometric materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrttL6foFVtlbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk9H8MzJF-mg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmt1Whu74%253D&amp;md5=4b0e9a529cd4c190542828ec5eff293c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/ja503622y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boucher, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaubicher, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cuisinier, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guyomard, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moreau, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Elucidation of the Na<sub>2/3</sub>FePO<sub>4</sub> and Li<sub>2/3</sub>FePO<sub>4</sub> Intermediate Superstructure Revealing a Pseudouniform Ordering in 2D</span>. <i>J. Here, we report layered NaVOPO4 as a cathode material that exhibits high voltage (â¼3.5 V vs. Na/Na+), high discharge capacity (144 mAh g-1 at 0.05 C), and remarkable cyclability with 67% capacity retention over 1,000 cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries attract increasing attention for large-scale energy storage as a promising alternative to the Li counterparts in view of low cost and abundant Na source.  However, the large ion radius of Na brings about challenging thermodn. and kinetic difficulties to the electrodes for Na-storage, including low reversible capacity and low ion transport, as well as large vol. change.  To mitigate or even overcome the kinetic problems, the authors develop a self-assembly route to a novel architecture consisting of nanosized porous NASICON-type NaTi2(PO4)3 particles embedded in microsized 3-dimensional graphene network.  Such architecture synergistically combines the advantages of a 3-dimensional graphene network and of 0-dimensional porous nanoparticles.  It greatly increases the electron/ion transport kinetics and assures the electrode structure integrity, leading to attractive electrochem. performance as reflected by a high rate-capability (112 mAh g-1 at 1C, 105 mAh g-1 at 5C, 96 mAh g-1 at 10C, 67 mAh g-1 at 50C), a long cycle-life (capacity retention of 80% after 1000 cycles at 10C), and a high initial Coulombic efficiency (&gt;79%).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Grid-scale energy storage systems with low-cost and high-performance electrodes are needed to meet the requirements of sustainable energy systems.  Due to the wide abundance and low cost of sodium resources and their similar electrochem. to the established lithium-ion batteries, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted considerable interest as ideal candidates for grid-scale energy storage systems.  In the past decade, though tremendous efforts have been made to promote the development of SIBs, and significant advances have been achieved, further improvements are still required in terms of energy/power d. and long cyclic stability for commercialization.  In this review, the latest progress in electrode materials for SIBs, including a variety of promising cathodes and anodes, is briefly summarized.  Besides, the sodium storage mechanisms, endeavors on electrochem. property enhancements, structural and compositional optimizations, challenges and perspectives of the electrode materials for SIBs are discussed.  Though enormous challenges may lie ahead, we believe that through intensive research efforts, sodium-ion batteries with low operation cost and longevity will be commercialized for large-scale energy storage application in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoo58FwhtNvWbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liuTfR8zH06iw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVaksbvK&amp;md5=1ef8733737aa6ee4f33eb1d4240e0c64</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2013.03.013"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Low-Cost and Environmentally Benign Aqueous Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Battery Based on NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>âNa<sub>2</sub>NiFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> Intercalation Chemistry</span>. <i>Electrochem. R. S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrolytes are an important component of electrochem. energy storage systems and their optimization is crit. for emerging beyond lithium ion technologies.  Here, an integrated computational-exptl. approach is used to rank-order and aid the selection of suitable electrolytes for a Na-ion battery.  We present an in silico strategy based on both thermodn. and kinetic descriptors derived from mol. dynamics simulations to rationally arrive at optimal electrolytes for Na-ion batteries.  We benchmarked various electrolytes (pure and binary mixts. of cyclic and acyclic carbonates with NaClO4 salt) to identify appropriate formulations with the overarching goal of simultaneously enhancing cell performance while meeting safety norms.  Fundamental insights from computationally derived thermodn. and kinetic data considerations coupled with atomistic-level description of the solvation dynamics is used to rank order the various electrolytes.  Thermodn. considerations based on free energy evaluation indicate EC:PC as a top electrolyte formulation under equil. conditions.  However, kinetic descriptors which are important factors dictating the rate capability and power performance suggest EC:DMC and EC:EMC to be among the best formulations.  Exptl. verification of these optimized formulations was carried out by examg. the electrochem. performance of various electrolytes in Na/TiO2 nanotubes half cells with NaClO4 salt.  Our rate capability studies confirm that EC:DMC and EC:EMC to be the best formulations.  These optimized formulations have low-rate specific capacities â¼120-140 mAh/g whereas the lower ranked electrolytes (EC: DEC) have capacities â¼95 mAh/g.  The various electrolytes are also evaluated from a safety perspective.  Such results suggest encouraging prospects for this approach in the a priori prediction of optimal sodium ion systems with possible screening implications for novel battery formulations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJZiypkQQpaLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liuTfR8zH06iw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXos1Wrt7Y%253D&amp;md5=22429c441999aebbb1dd0253e5e07e43</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.04.070"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Stable Linear Carbonate-Containing Electrolytes with Fluoroethylene Carbonate for High-Performance Cathodes in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly stable linear carbonate-containing electrolytes with fluoroethylene carbonate for high-performance cathodes in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Yongwon; Lee, Jaegi; Kim, Hyungsub; Kang, Kisuk; Choi, Nam-Soon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">320</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Employing linear carbonates such as di-Me carbonate (DMC), Et Me carbonate (EMC), and di-Et carbonate (DEC) as electrolyte solvents provides an opportunity to design appropriate electrolyte systems for high-performance sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, in practice, the use of linear carbonate-contg. electrolytes is quite challenging because linear carbonates readily decomp. at Na metal electrodes or sodiated anodes.  One of the promising approaches is using an electrolyte additive to resolve the crit. problems related to linear carbonates.  Our investigation reveals that remarkable enhancement in electrochem. performance of Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) cathodes with linear carbonate-contg. electrolytes is achieved by using a fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive.  Importantly, the initial Coulombic efficiency of the Na deposition/stripping on a stainless steel (SS) electrode is drastically improved from 16% to 90% by introducing the FEC additive into ethylene carbonate (EC)/propylene carbonate (PC)/DEC (5/3/2, vol./vol./v)/0.5 M NaClO4.  The underlying mechanism of FEC at the electrode-electrolyte interface is clearly demonstrated by 13C NMR (NMR).  In addn., the Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) cathode in EC/PC/DEC (5/3/2, vol./vol./v)/0.5 M sodium perchlorate (NaClO4) with FEC delivers a discharge capacity of 90.5 mAh g-1 at a current rate of C/2 and exhibits excellent capacity retention of 97.5% with high Coulombic efficiency of 99.6% after 300 cycles at 30 Â°C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpF8Wnh01Jj2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhSYJSVjNTaw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XmsFejtbg%253D&amp;md5=118f56bd8047e47cbbf45ae2943d84b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1039/c6cp07215a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cresce, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel thermally and electrochem. stable sodium ion conducting gel polymer electrolyte has been reported, which comprises a soln. of NaCF3SO3 (sodium triflate or NaTf) in a room temp. ionic liq. 1-Et 3-Me imidazolium trifluoro-methane sulfonate (EMI-triflate or EMITf) immobilized in poly (vinylidine fluoride-co-hexafluoropropylene) (PVdF-HFP).  Different structural, thermal, elec. and electrochem. studies demonstrate promising characteristics of the polymer films, suitable as electrolytes in rechargeable sodium batteries.  The possible conformational/structural changes in the polymer PVdF-HFP due to the entrapment of EMITf or EMITf/NaTf soln. have been investigated by Fourier transform infra-red (FTIR), scanning electron microscopic (SEM) and X-ray diffraction (XRD) techniques.  The electrolyte with the compn. of EMITf:PVdF-HFP (4:1 wt./wt.) + 0.5 M NaTf possesses excellent dimensional stability in the form of free standing thick film, which offers the ionic cond. of 5.74 Ã 10- 3 S cm- 1 at room temp. (â¼ 27 Â°C).  The temp. dependence of elec. cond. of polymer-ionic liq. blends and gel polymer electrolyte follows the Vogel-Tammen-Fulcher (VTF) behavior.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exptl. investigations on a sodium ion conducting gel polymer electrolyte nanocomposite based on poly(vinylidene fluoride-co-hexafluoropropylene) (PVdF-HFP), dispersed with silica nanoparticles are reported.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. were performed for the redn. decompn. of solvents widely used in Li-ion secondary battery electrolytes, ethylene carbonate (EC), propylene carbonate (PC), di-Me carbonate (DMC), Et Me carbonate (EMC), and di-Et carbonate (DEC), including a typical electrolyte additive, vinylene carbonate (VC), at the level of B3LYP/6-311+G(2d,p), both in the gas phase and soln. using the polarizable conductor calcn. model.  In the gas phase, the 1st electron redn. for the cyclic carbonates and for the linear carbonates is exothermic and endothermic, resp., while the 2nd electron redn. is endothermic for all the compds. examd.  On the contrary, in soln. both 1st and 2nd electron redns. are exothermic for all the compds.  Among the solvents and the additive examd., the likelihood of undergoing the 1st electron redn. in soln. was found in the order of EC &gt; PC &gt; VC &gt; DMC &gt; EMC &gt; DEC with EC being the most likely reduced.  VC, however, is most likely to undergo the 2nd electron redn. among the compds., in the order of VC &gt; EC &gt; PC.  Based on the results, the exptl. demonstrated effectiveness of VC as an excellent electrolyte additive was discussed.  The bulk thermodn. properties of two dilithium alkylene glycol dicarbonates, dilithium ethylene glycol dicarbonate (Li-EDC) and dilithium 1,2-propylene glycol dicarbonate (Li-PDC), as the major component of solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) films were also examd. through mol. dynamics (MD) simulations to understand the stability of the SEI film. Further, MD simulations of the interface between the decompn. compd. and graphite suggested that Li-EDC has more favorable interactions with the graphite surface than Li-PDC. 	{

	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){

<script nonce="90da907908e9b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

)|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {

    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
